    51→## Critical Rules
    52→
    53→### Storage Rules
    54→1. **NEVER** write files into `~/.claude/projects/*/memory/` — all memory goes to `./memory/`
    55→2. **NEVER** modify anything inside `source-repos/` — it is read-only reference
    56→3. **NEVER** store project specs, memory, or rules in `.claude/` — that dir is only for Claude-specific config (settings, skills)
    57→4. All specs, memory, rules, and artifacts go in the **project root** under their respective directories
    58→5. This ensures cross-platform portability (not tied to Claude's home directory)
    59→
    60→### Migration Rules
    61→6. Target Python code goes into `target-repos/` — this is where the migrated project grows
    62→7. Every spec document in `specs/` must cross-reference source files by relative path (e.g., `source-repos/ttrss-php/ttrss/classes/db.php`) rather than duplicating source code
    63→8. Specs may include **reasonable code examples** to highlight important architectural decisions, but must not be a copy of the source
    64→9. When migrating, always verify behavior parity against the source spec before marking a component complete
    65→
    66→### Source Traceability Rule (MANDATORY)
    67→10. **Every meaningful code element** (function, class, method, model, route, constant) in `target-repos/` **MUST** have a traceability comment linking it to its PHP source origin. This is a hard constraint — code without traceability comments must not be committed.
    68→
    69→    **Traceability comment format** (use the most specific match available):
    70→
    71→    ```python
    72→    # Source: ttrss/classes/feeds.php:Feeds::view (lines 45-120)
    73→    def view_feed(feed_id: int, view_mode: str) -> dict:
    74→        ...
    75→
    76→    # Source: ttrss/include/functions.php:catchup_feed (lines 1094-1237)
    77→    def catchup_feed(feed_id: int, cat_view: bool, ...) -> None:
    78→        ...
    79→
    80→    # Source: ttrss/classes/db.php:Db (singleton pattern)
    81→    # Python equivalent: SQLAlchemy engine via Flask-SQLAlchemy extension
    82→    db = SQLAlchemy(model_class=Base)
    83→
    84→    # Source: ttrss/schema/ttrss_schema_pgsql.sql (table ttrss_feeds, lines 38-72)
    85→    class Feed(Base):
    86→        __tablename__ = "ttrss_feeds"
    87→        ...
    88→    ```
    89→
    90→    **Match levels** (use the most specific that applies):
    91→    - **Direct**: `function → function` or `class → class` (e.g., `Feeds::view` → `view_feed()`)
    92→    - **Method-level**: `Class::method` → Python method (e.g., `RPC::mark` → `rpc.mark_article()`)
    93→    - **File-level**: When a Python module aggregates logic from a single PHP file (e.g., `# Source: ttrss/include/ccache.php`)
    94→    - **Multi-file**: When a Python module synthesizes logic from multiple PHP files (e.g., `# Source: ttrss/include/functions.php + ttrss/include/functions2.php (query building)`)
    95→    - **Schema-level**: For models derived from SQL schema (e.g., `# Source: ttrss/schema/ttrss_schema_pgsql.sql (table ttrss_user_entries)`)
    96→    - **Inferred**: When Python code has no direct PHP equivalent but was inferred from PHP patterns (e.g., `# Inferred from: ttrss/include/sessions.php (session validation pattern, adapted for Flask-Login)`)
    97→    - **New**: When code is genuinely new with no PHP source (e.g., `# New: no PHP equivalent (Alembic migration infrastructure)`)
    98→
    99→### Analysis Rules
   100→10. Use deep web research for any complicated architectural topic (PHP patterns, 3-tier architecture, ORM vs transactional script, etc.)
   101→11. For source code analysis dimensions (call graph, entity graph, etc.), consider using NetworkX and Leiden community detection
   102→12. Migration flow is driven by dimensions documented in `specs/10-migration-dimensions.md` — discuss and choose flow before starting migration
   103→
   104→### Quality Rules
   105→13. Preserve all functional behavior from the PHP source
   106→14. Fix known security issues during migration (SHA1→argon2id, prepared statements, etc.) — document deviations in specs
   107→15. Maintain spec-to-code traceability throughout the migration
   108→

    73→- **MODE2 format added**: PHP's current hash is `MODE2:{sha256(salt+password)}` using `ttrss_users.salt` column — was completely missing from original implementation.
    74→- `verify_password(stored_hash, password, salt="", login="")` — added `salt` and `login` params; `_handle_login` now passes `user.salt or ""` and `user.login`
    75→
    76→**PHP hash format reference** (from `ttrss/plugins/auth_internal/init.php` + `functions2.php:1481-1489`):
    77→- `SHA1:{hex}` — `sha1(password)` — no salt, legacy
    78→- `SHA1X:{hex}` — `sha1(login + ":" + password)` — LOGIN is the salt, colon separator, NO embedded salt in hash string
    79→- `MODE2:{hex}` — `sha256(ttrss_users.salt + password)` — modern, salt from DB column, no separator
    80→- `$argon2id$...` — Python migration upgrade (never in PHP)

    85→- SHA1X salt PREPENDED: `sha1(salt + password)` — CG-03 regression test in `tests/unit/test_password.py`

### Summary of Critical Traceability Points for Python Migration:

1. **Authentication Flow:**
   - `auth_internal/init.php:authenticate()` → calls `encrypt_password()` with logic detailed in functions2.php:1481
   - Uses salt-based SHA256 (MODE2) or SHA1 variants
   - API endpoint: `classes/api.php:login()` calls `authenticate_user()`

2. **Session Management:**
   - `include/sessions.php:validate_session()` validates IP, schema version, user agent, pwd_hash
   - Session storage in `ttrss_sessions` table with base64-encoded data
   - Lifetime controlled by `SESSION_COOKIE_LIFETIME`

3. **Database Schema (124 schema version):**
   - Primary entities: users, feeds, feed_categories, entries, user_entries, tags, labels2, enclosures
   - All foreign keys properly defined with cascade/set null
   - Session table for storing session data

4. **Key Data Structures:**
   - User: id, login, pwd_hash, salt, access_level, otp_enabled, last_login, email
   - Feed: owner_uid, title, feed_url, cat_id, auth_login, auth_pass, last_updated
   - Entry: guid, title, content, date_entered, lang, author
   - User_Entry: marked, published, unread, score, note, tag_cache, label_cache

All files have been verified and exist at their specified locations.

**Tool Call: Read specs and ADRs for traceability**
Status: Completed

## Summary Report: Specifications and Architecture Decision Records

I have read all 10 specification and decision documents. Here is a consolidated summary of **key requirements, constraints, and decisions** that should be traceable in the target code:

---

### **SPECIFICATIONS**

#### **1. specs/01-architecture.md — Architecture Patterns**

**Key Design Patterns:**
- Handler-based dispatch (NOT MVC) — classes act as controllers, DB queries embedded directly
- Raw SQL via `db_query()` adapter pattern (200+ call sites, no ORM in PHP)
- Server-rendered HTML fragments sent via JSON to frontend (AJAX RPC pattern)
- Plugin hook system with 24 hook types for extensibility
- Session-based authentication with IP/UA validation

**Entry Points:**
- `index.php` — Web UI (HTML + JS bootstrap)
- `backend.php` — AJAX RPC dispatcher (op, method dispatch)
- `api/index.php` — REST API (JSON, API level 8)
- `public.php` — Public feeds/login
- `update_daemon2.php` — Background feed update daemon

**Core Business Logic Locations:**
- `functions.php` (~2000 lines) — core utilities
- `functions2.php` (~2500 lines) — additional utilities
- `rssfuncs.php` (~1300 lines) — feed update engine

---

#### **2. specs/02-database.md — Table Definitions & Column Specs**

**35 Tables (5 core groups):**

| Group | Tables | Key Columns |
|-------|--------|-----------|
| **User Management** | ttrss_users, ttrss_sessions, ttrss_access_keys, ttrss_user_prefs, ttrss_settings_profiles | pwd_hash, salt, otp_enabled, access_level |
| **Feed Management** | ttrss_feeds, ttrss_feed_categories, ttrss_archived_feeds | owner_uid, feed_url, auth_login, auth_pass, cache_images, pubsub_state |
| **Articles** | ttrss_entries, ttrss_user_entries, ttrss_entry_comments, ttrss_enclosures | guid, content_hash, date_updated, ref_id, owner_uid |
| **Tagging/Labeling** | ttrss_tags, ttrss_labels2, ttrss_user_labels2 | tag_name, caption, fg_color, bg_color |
| **Filtering** | ttrss_filters2, ttrss_filters2_rules, ttrss_filters2_actions | match_any_rule, enabled, inverse, filter_type |

**Critical Schema Traits:**
- **Schema version 124** tracked in `ttrss_version.schema_version`
- **Multi-tenancy**: All user-scoped tables include `owner_uid` column (filtered at app layer, not DB)
- **Seed data**: Default admin user with SHA1 hash `"admin"` / `"password"`
- **Foreign key cascades**: Deletions cascade (user deletion → all feeds deleted)
- **Access pattern**: Raw SQL with `db_escape_string()`, no prepared statements, no ORM

---

#### **3. specs/03-api-routing.md — API Endpoints & Routing**

**Handler → Method Mapping (via backend.php ?op=X&method=Y):**

| op | Class | Key Methods |
|----|-------|-----------|
| `rpc` | RPC | mark, publ, delete, archive, getAllCounters, catchupSelected |
| `feeds` | Feeds | view, catchupAll, search, quickAddFeed |
| `article` | Article | view, redirect, editArticleTags, setScore |
| `pref-feeds` | Pref_Feeds | getfeedtree, editfeed, editSave, remove, addCat |
| `pref-filters` | Pref_Filters | edit, save, remove, testFilter |
| `pref-labels` | Pref_Labels | edit, save, remove |
| `pref-prefs` | Pref_Prefs | index, saveconfig, changepassword |
| `pref-users` | Pref_Users | edit, save, remove, resetPass (admin only) |

**CSRF Exemptions:**
- RPC: sanitycheck, completelabels
- Feeds: index, feedbrowser, quickaddfeed, search
- Article: redirect, editarticletags

**REST API (api/index.php):**
- **API level: 8**
- Authentication: `{"op":"login", "user":"...", "password":"..."}` → `{"session_id":"...", "api_level":8}`
- 30+ methods (getFeeds, getHeadlines, updateArticle, subscribeToFeed, etc.)
- Response format: `{"seq":0, "status":0, "content":{...}}`

---

#### **4. specs/06-security.md — Security Findings & Required Remediations**

**10 Critical/High Findings (to be fixed in migration):**

| # | Finding | Type | Remediation |
|---|---------|------|------------|
| **1** | SHA1 password hashing (broken) | CRITICAL | Replace with bcrypt/argon2id via passlib |
| **2** | SINGLE_USER_MODE auth bypass | CRITICAL | Remove or gate behind strong password requirement |
| **3** | mcrypt encryption (deprecated) | HIGH | Use Python cryptography (Fernet or AES-GCM) |
| **4** | SSL verification disabled (CURLOPT_SSL_VERIFYPEER=FALSE) | HIGH | Enable SSL cert validation in requests library |
| **5** | No prepared statements (db_escape_string only) | MEDIUM | Use SQLAlchemy parameterized queries |
| **6** | Weak CSRF tokens (uniqid+rand) | MEDIUM | Use secrets.token_hex() or framework-native CSRF |
| **7** | Missing security headers | MEDIUM | Add CSP, X-Frame-Options, HSTS middleware |
| **8** | Debug mode information disclosure ($_REQUEST["debug"]) | MEDIUM | Gate behind admin + dev environment flag |
| **9** | Inconsistent XSS protection (htmlspecialchars not universal) | MEDIUM | Use Jinja2 autoescape=True for all templates |
| **10** | Password hash stored in session | MEDIUM | Use session token validation instead |

**Session Architecture:**
- Custom PHP session handlers storing data in `ttrss_sessions` table (base64-encoded)
- Validation: IP (partial match), User-Agent SHA1, password hash, schema version
- IP validation strictness: 0=off, 1=first 3 octets, 2=first 2, 3=full
- Session timeout: `SESSION_COOKIE_LIFETIME` (default 86400s)
- Missing: SameSite cookie attribute

---

### **ARCHITECTURE DECISION RECORDS (ADRs)**

#### **ADR-0002: Python Framework — FLASK (Accepted)**

**Decision:** Flask + Flask-SQLAlchemy + Flask-Login + Flask-WTF + Celery

**Rationale:**
- Closest architectural match to PHP handler-based dispatch
- Blueprints map to handler classes naturally
- Jinja2 templates for HTML fragment rendering
- Synchronous web layer (async only in Celery workers for feed fetching)
- Flask-WTF provides session-based CSRF (zero frontend JS changes)
- Flask-Session + Redis for database-backed sessions
- No database: Flask-SQLAlchemy with sync psycopg2 driver

**Compliance Notes:**
- FastAPI rejected: async overkill for synchronous handler pattern
- CSRF: Flask-WTF session tokens preserve existing token mechanism
- Sessions: Flask-Session + Redis eliminates PHP manual garbage collection

---

#### **ADR-0003: Database Engine — PostgreSQL (Accepted)**

**Decision:** PostgreSQL only (migration from MySQL/MariaDB)

**Rationale:**
- Eliminates Sphinx full-text search dependency (PostgreSQL has native tsvector)
- Superior JSON support (JSONB columns for plugin storage)
- Better window functions, CTEs, concurrent write performance
- One-time pgloader migration acceptable

**Driver:** psycopg2 (sync, suitable for Flask WSGI)

**Alembic:** Manages all schema migrations going forward

---

#### **ADR-0006: ORM Strategy — SQLAlchemy ORM + Selective Core (Accepted)**

**Decision:**
- **Option A (Primary):** SQLAlchemy ORM — declarative models for all 35 tables with proper relationships
- **Option B (Selective):** SQLAlchemy Core for complex analytical queries (statistics, purge, score aggregation)

**Implementation:**
- Use `sqlacodegen` to auto-generate initial models from existing schema
- Alembic provides automated migration generation
- factory_boy enables test fixtures
- Replace 200+ raw SQL queries with ORM query API

**Hybrid Approach:**
- 90% of queries via ORM query builder
- 10% via SQLAlchemy Core for complex joins/aggregations

---

#### **ADR-0007: Session Management — Flask-Login + Redis (Accepted)**

**Decision:** Flask-Login + Flask-Session backed by Redis

**Architecture:**
- Flask-Login handles `@login_required`, `current_user`, remember-me
- Redis TTL eliminates manual garbage collection (replaces PHP cron)
- IP/UA validation via `before_request` hook
- API clients use separate API tokens (stored in DB, similar to `ttrss_api_sessions`)

**Key Features:**
- Session revocation instant (delete Redis key)
- Multi-instance scalability (shared Redis)
- Debugging via Redis CLI

**Infrastructure:** Redis shared with Celery (ADR-0011), adding no new dependencies

---

#### **ADR-0008: Password Hash Migration — Dual-Hash Gradual Migration (Accepted)**

**Decision:** Option A — transparent upgrade on login

**Migration Path:**
1. On login, detect hash format (SHA1, SHA1X, MODE2, or modern)
2. If legacy: verify with legacy algorithm, immediately re-hash with **argon2id**, update DB row
3. If modern: verify directly

**Hash Algorithm:** argon2id (via `argon2-cffi` library) for all new hashes

**Outcomes:**
- Active users upgrade transparently on next login
- Dormant accounts remain SHA1 until login or admin action
- Legacy SHA1 verification code maintained temporarily
- Monitoring query tracks migration progress: `SELECT count(*) WHERE pwd_hash LIKE 'sha1:%'`
- New user registrations always use argon2id

---

#### **ADR-0009: Feed Credential Encryption — Fernet (Accepted)**

**Decision:** Option A — Fernet (cryptography library)

**Migration Path:**
1. One-time script decrypts mcrypt-encrypted passwords via pycryptodome (AES-128-CBC)
2. Re-encrypt with Fernet using new key
3. Mark migrated rows with `fernet:` prefix for format detection

**Key Properties:**
- AES-128-CBC + HMAC-SHA256 (misuse-resistant)
- MultiFernet enables transparent key rotation without downtime
- Fernet tokens ~2x larger than raw ciphertext (base64 + HMAC + timestamp) — acceptable

**Rejected Alternatives:**
- AES-GCM: nonce misuse catastrophic, inappropriate for solo-dev
- mcrypt-compatible: perpetuates unauthenticated encryption vulnerable to padding oracle

---

### **TRACEABILITY CHECKLIST**

Items that **must appear in target code**:

**Configuration & Constants:**
- [ ] All 50+ config constants from config.php-dist (DB_TYPE, FEED_CRYPT_KEY, SINGLE_USER_MODE, etc.)
- [ ] Schema version tracking (ttrss_version.schema_version)
- [ ] Session cookie lifetime, IP validation strictness (SESSION_CHECK_ADDRESS 0-3)

**Database Models (SQLAlchemy ORM):**
- [ ] 35 table models with relationships
- [ ] owner_uid on all user-scoped tables (multi-tenancy enforcement)
- [ ] Foreign key cascade behavior matching PHP spec
- [ ] Seed data: default admin user (but hashed with argon2id, not SHA1)

**Security Implementations:**
- [ ] argon2id password hashing (new registrations + login upgrades)
- [ ] Legacy SHA1 verification code (temporary, for graceful migration)
- [ ] Fernet encryption for feed credentials (`fernet:` prefix)
- [ ] No SINGLE_USER_MODE or strong password gate
- [ ] SSL verification enabled for feed fetching (requests library defaults)
- [ ] Prepared statements everywhere (SQLAlchemy parameterization)
- [ ] CSRF tokens via Flask-WTF (secrets.token_hex internally)
- [ ] Security headers middleware (CSP, X-Frame-Options, HSTS, X-Content-Type-Options)
- [ ] Jinja2 autoescape=True for all templates
- [ ] SameSite cookie attribute (Flask-Session configuration)
- [ ] No debug parameter or restricted to admin + dev environment
- [ ] Session validation: no pwd_hash stored (use session token instead)

**Authentication & Sessions:**
- [ ] Flask-Login `@login_required` decorator
- [ ] Flask-Session + Redis backend
- [ ] IP/UA validation in `before_request` hook
- [ ] API token mechanism (separate from web sessions)
- [ ] Session expiry via Redis TTL

**Routing & Dispatch:**
- [ ] Handler/Blueprint structure mapping ?op=X&method=Y pattern

**Feed Update Daemon:**
- [ ] Celery workers for async feed fetching

**ORM/Query Patterns:**
- [ ] Declarative SQLAlchemy models (not raw SQL)
- [ ] sqlacodegen-generated initial models
- [ ] Alembic migrations for schema changes
- [ ] Selective SQLAlchemy Core for analytical queries
- [ ] factory_boy test fixtures

**Tool Call: Read target-repos/ttrss-python/ttrss/auth/password.py**
Status: Completed

```
     1→"""
     2→Password verification and hashing (ADR-0008, R10, AR04).
     3→
     4→Source: ttrss/plugins/auth_internal/init.php:Auth_Internal::authenticate
     5→        + Auth_Internal::check_password (lines 19-176)
     6→        + ttrss/include/functions2.php:encrypt_password (lines 1481-1489)
     7→
     8→PHP hash formats (from encrypt_password):
     9→  SHA1:<hex>        — sha1(password), no salt, legacy unsalted (old users, schema < 88)
    10→  SHA1X:<hex>       — sha1(login + ":" + password), LOGIN is the "salt", schema >= 88 without salt col
    11→  MODE2:<hex>       — sha256(ttrss_users.salt + password), salt from DB column, current default
    12→  $argon2id$...     — argon2id (Python migration: upgrade on first successful login, ADR-0008)
    13→
    14→Important: SHA1X embeds NO salt in the hash string itself. The "salt" for SHA1X is the
    15→user's login name, passed separately. The ttrss_users.salt column is only used for MODE2.
    16→
    17→Verification order (mirroring auth_internal authenticate() logic):
    18→1. argon2id  — upgraded/new passwords
    19→2. MODE2     — modern PHP salted SHA-256 (ttrss_users.salt column required)
    20→3. SHA1X     — legacy salted using login as salt with colon separator
    21→4. SHA1      — legacy unsalted (oldest TT-RSS installs)
    22→"""
    23→import hashlib
    24→
    25→from argon2 import PasswordHasher
    26→from argon2.exceptions import InvalidHashError, VerifyMismatchError
    27→
    28→# Source: ttrss/plugins/auth_internal/init.php (argon2id is the Python upgrade target)
    29→_ph = PasswordHasher()  # argon2id by default in argon2-cffi
    30→
    31→
    32→# Source: ttrss/plugins/auth_internal/init.php:Auth_Internal::change_password (new passwords)
    33→# AR04: SHA1/MODE2 are verify-only. All new/upgraded hashes use argon2id exclusively.
    34→def hash_password(password: str) -> str:
    35→    """Hash a new password with argon2id. Never SHA1/MODE2 for new passwords (AR04)."""
    36→    return _ph.hash(password)
    37→
    38→
    39→# Source: ttrss/plugins/auth_internal/init.php:Auth_Internal::authenticate (lines 19-140)
    40→#         + Auth_Internal::check_password (lines 142-176)
    41→#         + ttrss/include/functions2.php:encrypt_password (lines 1481-1489)
    42→def verify_password(
    43→    stored_hash: str,
    44→    password: str,
    45→    salt: str = "",
    46→    login: str = "",
    47→) -> bool:
    48→    """
    49→    Verify password against stored hash.
    50→    Returns True if valid, False otherwise.
    51→    Does not modify the stored hash — caller must call hash_password() + save after
    52→    a successful legacy verify to complete the ADR-0008 upgrade.
    53→
    54→    Args:
    55→        stored_hash: value from ttrss_users.pwd_hash
    56→        password:    plaintext password to verify
    57→        salt:        value from ttrss_users.salt (only needed for MODE2)
    58→        login:       value from ttrss_users.login (only needed for SHA1X)
    59→
    60→    PHP source equivalents:
    61→        argon2id: Python migration upgrade (no PHP counterpart)
    62→        MODE2:    encrypt_password($pass, $salt, true) → "MODE2:" . hash('sha256', $salt . $pass)
    63→        SHA1X:    encrypt_password($pass, $login) → "SHA1X:" . sha1("$login:$pass")
    64→        SHA1:     encrypt_password($pass) → "SHA1:" . sha1($pass)
    65→    """
    66→    if stored_hash.startswith("$argon2"):
    67→        try:
    68→            return _ph.verify(stored_hash, password)
    69→        except (VerifyMismatchError, InvalidHashError):
    70→            return False
    71→
    72→    if stored_hash.startswith("MODE2:"):
    73→        # Source: functions2.php:1484 — hash('sha256', $salt . $pass)
    74→        # salt is from ttrss_users.salt column, concatenated directly (no separator)
    75→        digest = stored_hash[6:]
    76→        expected = hashlib.sha256((salt + password).encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
    77→        return expected == digest
    78→
    79→    if stored_hash.startswith("SHA1X:"):
    80→        # Source: functions2.php:1485 — sha1("$login:$pass")
    81→        # The "salt" is the user's login name. Colon separator between login and password.
    82→        # The salt is NOT embedded in the stored_hash string — it comes from ttrss_users.login.
    83→        digest = stored_hash[6:]
    84→        expected = hashlib.sha1((login + ":" + password).encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
    85→        return expected == digest
    86→
    87→    if stored_hash.startswith("SHA1:"):
    88→        # Source: functions2.php:1487 — sha1($pass), no salt at all
    89→        digest = stored_hash[5:]
    90→        expected = hashlib.sha1(password.encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
    91→        return expected == digest
    92→
    93→    return False  # unknown hash format — reject
    94→
    95→
    96→def needs_upgrade(stored_hash: str) -> bool:
    97→    """
    98→    Return True if the stored hash should be upgraded to argon2id (ADR-0008).
    99→    All legacy formats (MODE2, SHA1X, SHA1) require upgrade.
   100→
   101→    Source: ttrss/plugins/auth_internal/init.php:Auth_Internal::authenticate
   102→            (lines 91-101 — upgrade to MODE2 on login; Python upgrades all the way to argon2id)
   103→    """
   104→    return not stored_hash.startswith("$argon2")
   105→
```

**Tool Call: Read target-repos/ttrss-python/ttrss/crypto/fernet.py**
Status: Completed

```
     1→"""
     2→Fernet encrypt/decrypt utilities (ADR-0009, R11, AR11).
     3→
     4→Source: ttrss/include/crypt.php:encrypt_string (lines 22-29)
     5→        + ttrss/include/crypt.php:decrypt_string (lines 2-20)
     6→        PHP used mcrypt_encrypt/decrypt (MCRYPT_RIJNDAEL_128) — replaced by Fernet (ADR-0009).
     7→
     8→The Fernet/MultiFernet instance is NOT instantiated here.
     9→It is created ONCE in create_app() from FEED_CRYPT_KEY env var,
    10→stored as app.config["FERNET"] (MultiFernet for key rotation per ADR-0009),
    11→and retrieved here via current_app.config["FERNET"].
    12→
    13→This ensures:
    14→- No key derivation in model code (AR11)
    15→- No env var reads at module import time
    16→- Testability via app fixture (pass a test Fernet in create_app(test_config=...))
    17→"""
    18→from flask import current_app
    19→
    20→
    21→# Source: ttrss/include/crypt.php:encrypt_string (lines 22-29)
    22→# PHP: mcrypt_encrypt(MCRYPT_RIJNDAEL_128, $key, $str, ...) → Python: Fernet.encrypt()
    23→def fernet_encrypt(plaintext: str) -> str:
    24→    """
    25→    Encrypt a string using the app-level MultiFernet instance (R11, ADR-0009).
    26→    Requires an active Flask application context.
    27→    """
    28→    f = current_app.config["FERNET"]
    29→    if f is None:
    30→        raise RuntimeError(
    31→            "FERNET not configured. Set FEED_CRYPT_KEY environment variable."
    32→        )
    33→    return f.encrypt(plaintext.encode("utf-8")).decode("ascii")
    34→
    35→
    36→# Source: ttrss/include/crypt.php:decrypt_string (lines 2-20)
    37→# PHP: mcrypt_decrypt(MCRYPT_RIJNDAEL_128, $key, $encstr, ...) → Python: Fernet.decrypt()
    38→def fernet_decrypt(token: str) -> str:
    39→    """
    40→    Decrypt a Fernet token using the app-level MultiFernet instance.
    41→    Raises cryptography.fernet.InvalidToken if the token is invalid or from a different key.
    42→    """
    43→    f = current_app.config["FERNET"]
    44→    if f is None:
    45→        raise RuntimeError(
    46→            "FERNET not configured. Set FEED_CRYPT_KEY environment variable."
    47→        )
    48→    return f.decrypt(token.encode("ascii")).decode("utf-8")
    49→

    31→        return str(e), 403
    32→

    35→        if request.path.startswith("/api/"):
    36→            return jsonify({"status": 1, "content": {"error": "NOT_FOUND"}}), 404
    37→        return str(e), 404
    38→

    41→        if request.path.startswith("/api/"):
    42→            return jsonify({"status": 1, "content": {"error": "INTERNAL_ERROR"}}), 500

    14→from flask_talisman import Talisman

    18→
    19→# Source: ttrss/classes/db.php:Db (singleton pattern)

**Tool Call: Read target-repos/ttrss-python/ttrss/blueprints/api/views.py**
Status: Completed

```
     1→"""
     2→TT-RSS REST API (/api/ — equivalent to PHP api/index.php).
     3→
     4→Source: ttrss/api/index.php (bootstrap + dispatch, lines 1-74)
     5→        + ttrss/classes/api.php:API (dispatch, wrap, login, logout, isLoggedIn, getVersion, getApiLevel)
     6→        + ttrss/include/functions.php:authenticate_user (lines 706-795)
     7→
     8→Protocol (spec/03-api-routing.md, R08, R09):
     9→  POST or GET /api/ with JSON body (or query params for GET).
    10→  Response envelope: {"seq": N, "status": 0|1, "content": {...}}
    11→  seq MUST be echoed from the request in every response (CG-04).
    12→  API level: 8.
    13→
    14→Auth (ADR-0007, ADR-0008, R07, AR05):
    15→  Login stores user_id in Redis session only — never pwd_hash (AR05).
    16→  Legacy MODE2/SHA1X/SHA1 hashes are upgraded to argon2id on first successful login (ADR-0008).
    17→"""
    18→from flask import Blueprint, jsonify, session
    19→from flask_login import current_user, login_user, logout_user
    20→
    21→from ttrss.auth.password import hash_password, needs_upgrade, verify_password
    22→from ttrss.extensions import db
    23→from ttrss.models.user import TtRssUser
    24→
    25→# Source: ttrss/api/index.php:1 (entry point), ttrss/classes/api.php:API (handler class)
    26→api_bp = Blueprint("api", __name__, url_prefix="/api")
    27→
    28→
    29→def _seq(data: dict) -> int:
    30→    """
    31→    Extract seq from request data — echoed in every response (CG-04, R08).
    32→    Source: ttrss/classes/api.php:API.__construct (line 26: $this->seq = (int) $_REQUEST['seq'])
    33→    """
    34→    from flask import request
    35→
    36→    return int(data.get("seq", request.args.get("seq", 0)))
    37→
    38→
    39→def _ok(seq: int, content: dict):
    40→    """
    41→    Success envelope. Source: ttrss/classes/api.php:API.wrap (lines 33-37, STATUS_OK=0).
    42→    """
    43→    return jsonify({"seq": seq, "status": 0, "content": content})
    44→
    45→
    46→def _err(seq: int, error: str):
    47→    """
    48→    Error envelope. Source: ttrss/classes/api.php:API.wrap (lines 33-37, STATUS_ERR=1).
    49→    """
    50→    return jsonify({"seq": seq, "status": 1, "content": {"error": error}})
    51→
    52→
    53→# Source: ttrss/api/index.php (method dispatch via $handler->$method())
    54→#         + ttrss/classes/api.php:API (method routing)
    55→@api_bp.route("/", methods=["GET", "POST"])
    56→def dispatch():
    57→    """Single dispatch endpoint for all API operations (spec/03-api-routing.md)."""
    58→    from flask import request
    59→
    60→    data = request.get_json(silent=True) or {}
    61→    op = data.get("op") or request.args.get("op", "")
    62→    seq = _seq(data)
    63→
    64→    if op == "login":
    65→        return _handle_login(data, seq)
    66→    if op == "logout":
    67→        # Source: ttrss/classes/api.php:API.logout (lines 89-92)
    68→        logout_user()
    69→        session.clear()
    70→        return _ok(seq, {"status": "OK"})
    71→    if op == "isLoggedIn":
    72→        # Source: ttrss/classes/api.php:API.isLoggedIn (lines 94-95)
    73→        # R09: content.status 1=logged in, 0=not logged in
    74→        return _ok(seq, {"status": 1 if current_user.is_authenticated else 0})
    75→    if op == "getVersion":
    76→        # Source: ttrss/classes/api.php:API.getVersion (lines 39-42)
    77→        return _ok(seq, {"version": "1.12.0-python"})
    78→    if op == "getApiLevel":
    79→        # Source: ttrss/classes/api.php:API.getApiLevel (lines 44-47)
    80→        return _ok(seq, {"level": 8})
    81→
    82→    # Source: ttrss/classes/api.php:API.__call (line 488 — UNKNOWN_METHOD error)
    83→    return _err(seq, "UNKNOWN_METHOD")
    84→
    85→
    86→def _handle_login(data: dict, seq: int):
    87→    """
    88→    Authenticate user and create session.
    89→    Upgrades legacy MODE2/SHA1X/SHA1 hash to argon2id on successful login (ADR-0008, R10).
    90→    Session stores user_id only — never pwd_hash (ADR-0007, R07, AR05).
    91→    Response includes session_id and api_level=8 (R08, spec/03-api-routing.md).
    92→
    93→    Source: ttrss/classes/api.php:API.login (lines 49-88)
    94→            + ttrss/include/functions.php:authenticate_user (lines 706-755)
    95→            + ttrss/plugins/auth_internal/init.php:Auth_Internal::authenticate (lines 19-140)
    96→    """
    97→    username = data.get("user", "")
    98→    password = data.get("password", "")
    99→
   100→    # Source: ttrss/plugins/auth_internal/init.php:authenticate — SELECT login, pwd_hash, salt
   101→    user: TtRssUser | None = db.session.scalars(
   102→        db.select(TtRssUser).where(TtRssUser.login == username)
   103→    ).first()
   104→
   105→    if not user or not verify_password(
   106→        user.pwd_hash,
   107→        password,
   108→        salt=user.salt or "",
   109→        login=user.login,
   110→    ):
   111→        # Source: ttrss/classes/api.php:API.login (line 68 — "LOGIN_ERROR")
   112→        return _err(seq, "LOGIN_ERROR")
   113→
   114→    # Upgrade legacy hash to argon2id on first successful login (ADR-0008)
   115→    # Source: ttrss/plugins/auth_internal/init.php:authenticate (lines 91-101 — MODE2 upgrade logic)
   116→    if needs_upgrade(user.pwd_hash):
   117→        user.pwd_hash = hash_password(password)
   118→        user.salt = None  # argon2id embeds its own salt; ttrss_users.salt no longer needed
   119→        db.session.commit()
   120→
   121→    # Source: ttrss/include/functions.php:authenticate_user (lines 724-739 — session setup)
   122→    login_user(user)
   123→    # AR05: store only user_id — pwd_hash MUST NOT be stored in session
   124→    # (contrast with PHP: $_SESSION["pwd_hash"] = ... — deliberately NOT replicated)
   125→    session["user_id"] = user.id
   126→
   127→    return _ok(
   128→        seq,
   129→        {
   130→            "session_id": getattr(session, "sid", ""),  # Flask-Session sets .sid
   131→            "api_level": 8,
   132→        },
   133→    )
   134→
```

    20→class TtRssFeed(Base):
    21→    """
    22→    Feed subscription record.
    23→    auth_pass is stored Fernet-encrypted at rest (ADR-0009, R11).
    24→    AR11: Fernet instance is NOT derived here — accessed via current_app.config["FERNET"]
    25→    through ttrss.crypto.fernet helpers.
    26→    """
    27→

    29→

    32→    title: Mapped[Optional[str]] = mapped_column(String(200))

    34→    site_url: Mapped[Optional[str]] = mapped_column(String(250))
    35→    last_updated: Mapped[Optional[datetime]] = mapped_column(DateTime)
    36→    update_interval: Mapped[int] = mapped_column(Integer, nullable=False, default=0)
    37→    cat_id: Mapped[Optional[int]] = mapped_column(Integer)

    39→    _auth_pass: Mapped[Optional[str]] = mapped_column("auth_pass", Text)
    40→    last_error: Mapped[Optional[str]] = mapped_column(String(250))
    41→    cache_images: Mapped[bool] = mapped_column(Boolean, nullable=False, default=False)
    42→    pubsub_state: Mapped[int] = mapped_column(Integer, nullable=False, default=0)
    43→
    44→    @property
    45→    def auth_pass(self) -> Optional[str]:
    46→        """Decrypt feed password from Fernet-encrypted column (ADR-0009, R11)."""
    47→        if self._auth_pass is None:
    48→            return None
    49→        from ttrss.crypto.fernet import fernet_decrypt
    50→
    51→        return fernet_decrypt(self._auth_pass)
    52→
    53→    @auth_pass.setter
    54→    def auth_pass(self, value: Optional[str]) -> None:
    55→        """Encrypt feed password before writing to column (ADR-0009, R11)."""
    56→        if value is None:
    57→            self._auth_pass = None
    58→        else:
    59→            from ttrss.crypto.fernet import fernet_encrypt
    60→
    61→            self._auth_pass = fernet_encrypt(value)
    62→

**Tool Call: Read target-repos/ttrss-python/tests/unit/test_password.py**
Status: Completed

```
     1→"""
     2→Pure function tests for ttrss.auth.password (ADR-0008, R10, AR04).
     3→No database required — these functions operate on strings only.
     4→AR07-compliant: AR07 prohibits SQLite as DB substitute, not the absence of a DB
     5→when none is genuinely needed.
     6→
     7→Source coverage:
     8→  ttrss/plugins/auth_internal/init.php:Auth_Internal::authenticate (all hash format branches)
     9→  ttrss/include/functions2.php:encrypt_password (lines 1481-1489)
    10→
    11→PHP hash format reference (functions2.php:1481-1489):
    12→  SHA1:<hex>    — sha1($pass), no salt
    13→  SHA1X:<hex>   — sha1("$login:$pass"), login is the "salt", colon separator
    14→  MODE2:<hex>   — hash('sha256', $salt . $pass), salt from ttrss_users.salt column, no separator
    15→"""
    16→import hashlib
    17→
    18→from ttrss.auth.password import hash_password, needs_upgrade, verify_password
    19→
    20→
    21→def test_hash_password_produces_argon2id():
    22→    h = hash_password("testpassword")
    23→    assert h.startswith("$argon2id$"), "hash_password must produce argon2id hash (AR04)"
    24→
    25→
    26→def test_verify_argon2id_correct():
    27→    h = hash_password("correcthorse")
    28→    assert verify_password(h, "correcthorse") is True
    29→
    30→
    31→def test_verify_argon2id_wrong():
    32→    h = hash_password("correcthorse")
    33→    assert verify_password(h, "wrongpassword") is False
    34→
    35→
    36→# --- MODE2 tests (functions2.php:1484: hash('sha256', $salt . $pass)) ---
    37→
    38→def test_verify_mode2_correct():
    39→    """MODE2: sha256(salt + password), no separator. Source: functions2.php:1484."""
    40→    salt = "abc123salt"
    41→    password = "hunter2"
    42→    digest = hashlib.sha256((salt + password).encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
    43→    stored = f"MODE2:{digest}"
    44→    assert verify_password(stored, password, salt=salt) is True
    45→
    46→
    47→def test_verify_mode2_wrong_password():
    48→    salt = "abc123salt"
    49→    password = "correct"
    50→    digest = hashlib.sha256((salt + password).encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
    51→    stored = f"MODE2:{digest}"
    52→    assert verify_password(stored, "wrong", salt=salt) is False
    53→
    54→
    55→def test_verify_mode2_wrong_salt():
    56→    """MODE2: wrong salt must not verify — salt is from ttrss_users.salt column."""
    57→    salt = "correctsalt"
    58→    password = "password"
    59→    digest = hashlib.sha256((salt + password).encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
    60→    stored = f"MODE2:{digest}"
    61→    assert verify_password(stored, password, salt="wrongsalt") is False
    62→
    63→
    64→# --- SHA1X tests (functions2.php:1485: sha1("$login:$pass")) ---
    65→
    66→def test_verify_sha1x_login_as_salt_with_colon():
    67→    """SHA1X: sha1(login + ':' + password). Source: functions2.php:1485."""
    68→    login = "testuser"
    69→    password = "hunter2"
    70→    digest = hashlib.sha1((login + ":" + password).encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
    71→    stored = f"SHA1X:{digest}"
    72→    assert verify_password(stored, password, login=login) is True
    73→
    74→
    75→def test_verify_sha1x_wrong_password():
    76→    login = "testuser"
    77→    password = "correct"
    78→    digest = hashlib.sha1((login + ":" + password).encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
    79→    stored = f"SHA1X:{digest}"
    80→    assert verify_password(stored, "wrong", login=login) is False
    81→
    82→
    83→def test_verify_sha1x_wrong_login():
    84→    """SHA1X: wrong login must not verify — login is the salt for SHA1X."""
    85→    login = "correctuser"
    86→    password = "password"
    87→    digest = hashlib.sha1((login + ":" + password).encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
    88→    stored = f"SHA1X:{digest}"
    89→    assert verify_password(stored, password, login="wronguser") is False
    90→
    91→
    92→def test_verify_sha1x_no_embedded_salt_in_hash():
    93→    """
    94→    SHA1X hash string is 'SHA1X:{40-hex}' — the salt is NOT embedded in the hash.
    95→    The old implementation wrongly expected 'SHA1X:{salt}:{digest}' (3 parts).
    96→    Source: functions2.php:1485 — return "SHA1X:" . sha1("$login:$pass")
    97→    """
    98→    login = "admin"
    99→    password = "password"
   100→    digest = hashlib.sha1((login + ":" + password).encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
   101→    stored = f"SHA1X:{digest}"
   102→    # stored has exactly 2 colon-separated parts: prefix and digest
   103→    parts = stored.split(":")
   104→    assert len(parts) == 2, "SHA1X hash must be 'SHA1X:{digest}' — no embedded salt"
   105→    assert verify_password(stored, password, login=login) is True
   106→
   107→
   108→# --- SHA1 unsalted tests (functions2.php:1487: sha1($pass)) ---
   109→
   110→def test_verify_sha1_unsalted():
   111→    """Legacy unsalted SHA1 (oldest TT-RSS installs). Source: functions2.php:1487."""
   112→    password = "legacy"
   113→    digest = hashlib.sha1(password.encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
   114→    stored = f"SHA1:{digest}"
   115→    assert verify_password(stored, password) is True
   116→
   117→
   118→def test_verify_sha1_unsalted_wrong():
   119→    password = "legacy"
   120→    digest = hashlib.sha1(password.encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
   121→    stored = f"SHA1:{digest}"
   122→    assert verify_password(stored, "wrong") is False
   123→
   124→
   125→# --- needs_upgrade tests ---
   126→
   127→def test_needs_upgrade_mode2_returns_true():
   128→    salt = "s"
   129→    digest = hashlib.sha256(("s" + "p").encode()).hexdigest()
   130→    assert needs_upgrade(f"MODE2:{digest}") is True
   131→
   132→
   133→def test_needs_upgrade_sha1x_returns_true():
   134→    digest = hashlib.sha1(("user:p").encode()).hexdigest()
   135→    assert needs_upgrade(f"SHA1X:{digest}") is True
   136→
   137→
   138→def test_needs_upgrade_sha1_returns_true():
   139→    digest = hashlib.sha1(b"p").hexdigest()
   140→    assert needs_upgrade(f"SHA1:{digest}") is True
   141→
   142→
   143→def test_needs_upgrade_argon2id_returns_false():
   144→    h = hash_password("p")
   145→    assert needs_upgrade(h) is False
   146→
   147→
   148→# --- unknown format rejection ---
   149→
   150→def test_verify_unknown_format_rejected():
   151→    assert verify_password("PLAINTEXT:password", "password") is False
   152→    assert verify_password("md5:5f4dcc3b5aa765d61d8327deb882cf99", "password") is False
   153→    assert verify_password("", "password") is False
   154→
```

**Tool Call: Read target-repos/ttrss-python/alembic/env.py**
Status: Completed

```
     1→"""
     2→Alembic migration environment.
     3→target_metadata = Base.metadata ensures autogenerate sees all 10 models (CG-06, R06).
     4→DATABASE_URL is read from environment — not from alembic.ini (R03, AR01).
     5→
     6→New: no PHP equivalent — Alembic replaces ttrss/classes/dbupdater.php:DbUpdater
     7→     (PHP ran raw SQL version upgrade files in ttrss/schema/versions/pgsql/*.sql;
     8→     Alembic generates and applies migrations from ORM metadata instead).
     9→Source schema baseline: ttrss/schema/ttrss_schema_pgsql.sql
    10→"""
    11→import os
    12→from logging.config import fileConfig
    13→
    14→from alembic import context
    15→from sqlalchemy import engine_from_config, pool
    16→
    17→config = context.config
    18→
    19→if config.config_file_name is not None:
    20→    fileConfig(config.config_file_name)
    21→
    22→# Import all models so they register with Base.metadata before autogenerate runs
    23→import ttrss.models  # noqa: F401 — side-effect import; registers all 10 mappers
    24→from ttrss.models.base import Base
    25→
    26→target_metadata = Base.metadata  # CG-06: single metadata for all 10 tables
    27→
    28→
    29→def get_url() -> str:
    30→    url = os.environ.get("DATABASE_URL")
    31→    if url:
    32→        return url
    33→    return config.get_main_option("sqlalchemy.url", "")
    34→
    35→
    36→def run_migrations_offline() -> None:
    37→    url = get_url()
    38→    context.configure(
    39→        url=url,
    40→        target_metadata=target_metadata,
    41→        literal_binds=True,
    42→        dialect_opts={"paramstyle": "named"},
    43→    )
    44→    with context.begin_transaction():
    45→        context.run_migrations()
    46→
    47→
    48→def run_migrations_online() -> None:
    49→    configuration = config.get_section(config.config_ini_section, {})
    50→    configuration["sqlalchemy.url"] = get_url()
    51→    connectable = engine_from_config(
    52→        configuration,
    53→        prefix="sqlalchemy.",
    54→        poolclass=pool.NullPool,
    55→    )
    56→    with connectable.connect() as connection:
    57→        context.configure(
    58→            connection=connection,
    59→            target_metadata=target_metadata,
    60→        )
    61→        with context.begin_transaction():
    62→            context.run_migrations()
    63→
    64→
    65→if context.is_offline_mode():
    66→    run_migrations_offline()
    67→else:
    68→    run_migrations_online()
    69→
```

| pwd_hash | varchar(250) NOT NULL | String(256) | Size: 250→256 |
| last_login | timestamp default null | DateTime | ✓ OK |
| access_level | integer NOT NULL default 0 | Integer NOT NULL default=0 | ✓ OK |


| email | varchar(250) NOT NULL default '' | MISSING | |
| full_name | varchar(250) NOT NULL default '' | MISSING | |
| email_digest | boolean NOT NULL default false | MISSING | |
| last_digest_sent | timestamp default null | MISSING | |
| salt | varchar(250) NOT NULL default '' | String(256) nullable | Size 250→256 + nullability wrong (PHP: NOT NULL default '', Python: nullable) |
| twitter_oauth | text default null | MISSING | |
| otp_enabled | boolean NOT NULL default=False | ✓ OK | |
| resetpass_token | varchar(250) default null | MISSING |

I'm seeing several fields completely missing from the Python models—email, full_name, email_digest, last_digest_sent, twitter_oauth, and resetpass_token—plus the salt field has both a size mismatch and incorrect nullability handling.

Now I'm checking the TtRssFeedCategory table and finding that owner_uid is missing its foreign key constraint, collapsed and view_settings aren't in Python at all, and parent_cat is also missing its self-referential foreign key. The title field size changed from 200 to 250 characters.

Continuing through TtRssFeed... I'm noticing several more mismatches in the schema mapping—the auth fields are marked as Optional in Python but have NOT NULL constraints in the database, and there are quite a few columns missing from the ORM model entirely like icon_url, purge_interval, favicon_avg_color, and various display/update settings.

Now looking at the TtRssEntry table, I'm seeing a similar pattern where core fields like title, guid, link, updated, and content are all NOT NULL in PHP but mapped as Optional in Python, plus there's a no_orig_date column that's completely missing from the Python model. Continuing through the TtRssUserEntry table schema, I'm checking the remaining columns for consistency between the PHP and Python implementations—looking at foreign key constraints, data types, and nullable fields to identify where the Python model is missing definitions or has type mismatches.

Now examining the TtRssEnclosure table, which has several nullability issues where PHP defines NOT NULL constraints but the Python model allows optional values, plus a phantom column in Python that doesn't exist in the original PHP schema.

Continuing through TtRssLabel2, I'm seeing color field size mismatches—the PHP schema uses varchar(15) but Python constrains them to String(10)—and missing foreign key constraints in the Python implementation. The TtRssUserLabel2 table shows label_id as a primary key in Python while PHP treats it as a foreign key. OK so I have a comprehensive list. The major issues are critical correctness problems: `TtRssUser.login` needs to be shortened to 120 characters, `created_time` should be renamed to `created`, and `salt` should have a non-nullable default empty string. Several fields need type changes — `feed_url` and `link` should be Text instead of String, `guid` should be Text with NOT NULL and UNIQUE constraints, and `duration` in enclosures should be Text. I also need to mark `title` fields as NOT NULL in both feeds and entries, and remove the phantom `width` and `height` columns from enclosures.

Beyond those, there are more adjustments: color fields need to be String(15) instead of String(10), `score` should be Integer not SmallInteger, and `note` should be Text. There are various nullability mismatches to address, and `TtRssFeedCategory.title` should be String(200) not String(250). I'm also noting several missing columns across the tables — user fields like email and full_name, category settings, and feed properties like icon_url and purge_interval — but I'm deferring those to Phase 1a with traceability notes since they're not critical correctness issues.

Actually, reconsidering this: for a walking skeleton, I should add all the missing columns now. The models need to match the database schema completely, otherwise the ORM won't handle those fields correctly and Alembic migrations will be incomplete. This is the foundational layer, so getting it right from the start makes sense.

The nullability question is trickier though—the PHP schema has many `NOT NULL` constraints with defaults, but making those Optional in Python avoids insert failures during Phase 1a when we're not populating those columns yet. However, for true schema correctness and to match what Alembic will generate, I should align with the actual database constraints.

Let me go ahead and apply all the fixes across the files: matching every type, size, nullability, and column name to the PHP schema, plus adding the comprehensive traceability comments.

    User account table.
    Flask-Login UserMixin provides: get_id(), is_active, is_authenticated, is_anonymous.

    # ADR-0009: In Python all auth_pass values are Fernet-encrypted; this flag tracks
    # whether PHP-era mcrypt encryption was already applied (migration marker).
    auth_pass_encrypted: Mapped[bool] = mapped_column(Boolean, nullable=False, default=False)

    @property
    def auth_pass(self) -> str:
        """
        Decrypt feed password from Fernet-encrypted column (ADR-0009, R11).
        Source: ttrss/include/crypt.php:decrypt_string (lines 2-20) → Fernet.decrypt()
        Returns empty string if column is empty (matches PHP default '').
        """
        if not self._auth_pass:
            return ""
        from ttrss.crypto.fernet import fernet_decrypt

        return fernet_decrypt(self._auth_pass)

    @auth_pass.setter
    def auth_pass(self, value: str | None) -> None:
        """
        Encrypt feed password before writing to column (ADR-0009, R11).
        Source: ttrss/include/crypt.php:encrypt_string (lines 22-29) → Fernet.encrypt()
        """
        if not value:
            self._auth_pass = ""
        else:
            from ttrss.crypto.fernet import fernet_encrypt

            self._auth_pass = fernet_encrypt(value)

## Adversarial Self-Refine: Round 1 — CRITIC

Now launching the CRITIC agent in isolation to find everything I missed:

**Tool Call: CRITIC Round 1: compliance review**
Status: Completed

Now I have all the information needed for a thorough compliance review. Here is the complete finding list:

---

## NON-COMPLIANCE FINDINGS

### Schema Correctness Flaws

**1.** `ttrss_version` model (`version.py` line 31): `schema_version` is declared as `primary_key=True`. The PHP schema (line 262) defines it as `schema_version int not null` with NO primary key. This is a phantom constraint -- SQLAlchemy requires a PK, but the model adds one that does not exist in the source schema, and no `# New:` or `# Inferred from:` comment explains this deviation.

**2.** `ttrss_user_entries` model (`user_entry.py` line 36): `uuid` has `default=""`. The PHP schema (line 159) defines `uuid varchar(200) not null` with NO default. An empty-string default is a phantom default that does not exist in the source schema.

**3.** `ttrss_user_entries` model (`user_entry.py` line 38): `feed_id` is missing `index=True`. The PHP schema has explicit index `ttrss_user_entries_feed_id` (line 177). The `unread` column (line 67) is also missing `index=True` per PHP schema line 178.

**4.** `ttrss_entries` model (`entry.py` lines 50-52): `date_entered` has `server_default=func.now()`. The PHP schema (line 143) defines `date_entered timestamp not null` with NO default. This is a phantom server default.

**5.** `ttrss_feeds` model (`feed.py` line 46): `cat_id` is missing `index=True`. The PHP schema explicitly creates `ttrss_feeds_cat_id_idx` (line 102).

**6.** `ttrss_tags` model (`tag.py`): `owner_uid` is missing `index=True` (PHP schema line 259: `ttrss_tags_owner_uid_index`). `post_int_id` is missing `index=True` (PHP schema line 260: `ttrss_tags_post_int_id_idx`).

**7.** `ttrss_enclosures` model (`enclosure.py`): `post_id` is missing `index=True` (PHP schema line 273: `ttrss_enclosures_post_id_idx`).

**8.** `ttrss_entries` model (`entry.py`): `guid` is missing `index=True` for the explicit index `ttrss_entries_guid_index` (PHP schema line 151). While `unique=True` implicitly creates an index in most databases, the PHP schema explicitly creates a separate index. `date_entered` is missing `index=True` (PHP schema line 153: `ttrss_entries_date_entered_index`). `updated` is missing `index=True` (PHP schema line 154: `ttrss_entries_updated_idx`).

**9.** `ttrss_user_entries` model (`user_entry.py`): `ref_id` has `index=True` which is correct, but `feed_id` and `unread` are missing their indexes as noted in finding 3.

**10.** All models are missing SQLAlchemy `ForeignKey` declarations. The PHP schema defines foreign key constraints on: `ttrss_feeds.owner_uid` -> `ttrss_users(id)`, `ttrss_feeds.cat_id` -> `ttrss_feed_categories(id)`, `ttrss_feeds.parent_feed` -> `ttrss_feeds(id)`, `ttrss_feed_categories.owner_uid` -> `ttrss_users(id)`, `ttrss_feed_categories.parent_cat` -> `ttrss_feed_categories(id)`, `ttrss_user_entries.ref_id` -> `ttrss_entries(id)`, `ttrss_user_entries.feed_id` -> `ttrss_feeds(id)`, `ttrss_user_entries.orig_feed_id` -> `ttrss_archived_feeds(id)`, `ttrss_user_entries.owner_uid` -> `ttrss_users(id)`, `ttrss_tags.owner_uid` -> `ttrss_users(id)`, `ttrss_tags.post_int_id` -> `ttrss_user_entries(int_id)`, `ttrss_enclosures.post_id` -> `ttrss_entries(id)`, `ttrss_labels2.owner_uid` -> `ttrss_users(id)`, `ttrss_user_labels2.label_id` -> `ttrss_labels2(id)`, `ttrss_user_labels2.article_id` -> `ttrss_entries(id)`. None of these ForeignKey constraints are declared in the SQLAlchemy models. The docstrings mention them but the column definitions do not enforce them.

**11.** All models are missing `ondelete` cascade specifications. The PHP schema specifies `ON DELETE CASCADE` or `ON DELETE SET NULL` on every foreign key. Without `ForeignKey` declarations, these cascade behaviors are absent from the ORM layer entirely.

**12.** `ttrss_user_entries` model: The PHP schema (line 165) defines `tag_cache text not null` and `label_cache text not null` with NO defaults. The Python model (lines 50, 53) adds `default=""` to both. These are phantom defaults.

### Source Traceability Flaws

**13.** `ttrss/auth/session.py` is an empty file (only a docstring, no code). It contains no `user_loader` or session logic. The actual `user_loader` callback lives in `ttrss/extensions.py` (lines 42-47). The session module's existence is misleading -- it declares itself a session utility module but contains zero code elements.

**14.** `ttrss/errors.py`: The inner functions `bad_request`, `unauthorized`, `forbidden`, `not_found`, `server_error` are each missing individual traceability comments. They are meaningful code elements (error handlers) per Rule 10. The parent function has a generic `# Inferred from:` comment, but each handler maps to a distinct PHP behavior (e.g., `NOT_LOGGED_IN` comes from `api.php:API.__construct` line 17, but the 400/403/404/500 handlers have no PHP source mapping at all).

**15.** `ttrss/config.py`: The `Config` class attributes `SQLALCHEMY_TRACK_MODIFICATIONS`, `SQLALCHEMY_ENGINE_OPTIONS`, `SESSION_USE_SIGNER`, `SESSION_COOKIE_HTTPONLY`, `SESSION_COOKIE_SAMESITE`, `SESSION_COOKIE_LIFETIME`, `WTF_CSRF_ENABLED`, `WTF_CSRF_HEADERS` all lack `# New:` traceability comments. They are meaningful constants with no PHP equivalent and require `# New:` annotations per Rule 10.

**16.** `ttrss/extensions.py` line 37: `login_manager.login_view = "public.index"` is a meaningful configuration constant with no traceability comment. It should have a `# New:` comment.

### API Response Format Flaws

**17.** `ttrss/errors.py`: All error handler responses (lines 17, 24, 30, 36, 42) are missing the `seq` field in the JSON envelope. The requirement states the API response format MUST be `{"seq":N, "status":0|1, "content":{...}}`. The error handlers return `{"status": 1, "content": {"error": ...}}` without `seq`. This violates the API response format requirement.

**18.** `ttrss/blueprints/api/views.py` line 74: The `isLoggedIn` response returns `{"status": 1 if ... else 0}` inside `content`. In the PHP source (`api.php` lines 94-95), this returns `{"status":true}` or `{"status":false}` as boolean values, not integers. The Python code uses integers 1/0, which is a behavioral divergence from the PHP source.

### Code Logic Flaws

**19.** `ttrss/blueprints/api/views.py` lines 55-83: The `dispatch()` function accepts GET requests (`methods=["GET", "POST"]`). The PHP `api/index.php` processes `$_REQUEST` which includes both GET and POST, but the actual API protocol specification says "POST or GET /api/ with JSON body". GET requests with `request.get_json()` will typically return `None` because GET requests do not carry JSON bodies. The fallback to `request.args.get("op", "")` partially handles this, but `_seq()` extracts `seq` from `data` (the JSON body) first, which will be empty `{}` for GET requests, making seq extraction fragile.

**20.** `ttrss/blueprints/api/views.py` line 69: The `logout` handler calls `session.clear()` which is a Flask session operation. However, the API is supposed to be exempt from CSRF (PHP API has no CSRF protection -- it uses session ID tokens instead). There is no `csrf.exempt` decorator on the `api_bp` blueprint or the `dispatch` route. This means API POST requests will be rejected by Flask-WTF CSRFProtect unless a CSRF token is provided, which the PHP API never required.

**21.** `ttrss/__init__.py` line 32: `FEED_CRYPT_KEY` is read via `app.config.get("FEED_CRYPT_KEY", b"")`. However, in `config.py` line 31, `FEED_CRYPT_KEY` is set as `os.environ.get("FEED_CRYPT_KEY", "").encode()`. If the environment variable is set to a valid Fernet key, this works. But `Fernet()` requires a base64-encoded 32-byte key. The code does not validate the key format before passing it to `Fernet()`, which will raise an exception at application startup if the key is present but malformed. There is no graceful error message.

**22.** `ttrss/blueprints/backend/views.py` line 30: The dispatch function reads from `request.form` first, then `data` (JSON). The PHP `backend.php` reads from `$_REQUEST` which merges GET, POST, and COOKIE. The Python implementation does not read from `request.args` (query parameters), which is a behavioral divergence from PHP `$_REQUEST`.

### Over-Engineering / Scope Concerns

**23.** `ttrss/__init__.py` line 44: `Talisman` is initialized with `content_security_policy=False`. Talisman adds HSTS, X-Content-Type-Options, X-Frame-Options, and other security headers. The PHP TT-RSS has no equivalent security header middleware. While security headers are generally good, introducing `flask-talisman` as a hard dependency in Phase 1a is scope creep beyond the stated migration requirements. There is no ADR or spec requirement for Talisman beyond a brief mention of "G4/ADR-0002 requirements" in a comment.

**24.** `ttrss/models/user_entry.py` line 36: The `uuid` column has `default=""` added. The PHP schema defines `uuid varchar(200) not null` without a default. Adding a default empty string silently changes the schema contract -- PHP code that inserts into `ttrss_user_entries` is required to supply a `uuid` value, but the Python model allows omitting it.

### Missing Model Features

**25.** No SQLAlchemy `relationship()` declarations exist on any model. While foreign keys are themselves missing (finding 10), even if they were present, there are no ORM relationships defined between `TtRssUser` and `TtRssFeed`, `TtRssFeed` and `TtRssEntry`, `TtRssEntry` and `TtRssUserEntry`, etc. This means all queries must be written with explicit joins rather than using ORM navigation. This is not necessarily a schema correctness issue, but it means the ORM layer is functioning as a glorified table definition rather than an object-relational mapper.

**26.** `ttrss/models/feed.py` lines 112-136: The `auth_pass` property getter/setter imports `fernet_encrypt`/`fernet_decrypt` inside the method body. These imports require a Flask application context (`current_app`). This means the model cannot be used outside a Flask request context (e.g., in a CLI script or background worker) without explicitly pushing an app context. The PHP code has no such constraint -- `crypt.php` functions are globally available.

### Test Coverage Flaws

**27.** `tests/unit/test_password.py`: There is no test for the `verify_password` function when `stored_hash` starts with `$argon2` but is a malformed/corrupted argon2 hash (not just a mismatch). The `InvalidHashError` exception path (password.py line 69) is not covered.

**28.** `tests/unit/test_password.py`: There is no test verifying that `hash_password` output can be verified by `verify_password` when `needs_upgrade` returns `False` -- i.e., the round-trip test `hash -> verify -> needs_upgrade==False` as a single assertion chain is absent.

**29.** `tests/unit/test_password.py`: There is no test for `verify_password` with the PHP seed hash `SHA1:5baa61e4c9b93f3f0682250b6cf8331b7ee68fd8` (which is SHA1 of "password") from the schema seed data (line 55-56). This is the most critical real-world test case -- verifying the admin default password.

### Alembic Configuration Flaws

**30.** `alembic/env.py` line 33: `get_url()` falls back to `config.get_main_option("sqlalchemy.url", "")`. If neither `DATABASE_URL` env var nor `alembic.ini` URL is set, this returns an empty string, which will cause a cryptic SQLAlchemy error rather than a clear failure message. The PHP equivalent (`db.php`) validates the DB connection parameters before attempting connection.

### Session Handling Flaws

**31.** `ttrss/blueprints/api/views.py` line 131: `session.sid` is accessed via `getattr(session, "sid", "")`. Flask-Session's `sid` attribute is the server-side session identifier. The PHP API returns the session ID as a string that the client must pass back in subsequent API requests (via `sid` parameter). The Python code stores `user_id` in the session (line 126) and returns `session.sid`, but there is no code anywhere that validates an incoming `sid` parameter on subsequent API calls. The PHP API validates the session ID on every request via `$_SESSION` mechanics. The Python code relies entirely on Flask-Login's cookie-based session, which means the `session_id` returned to the API client is useless -- there is no mechanism for API clients to authenticate subsequent requests using this session ID.

**32.** `ttrss/auth/session.py`: This file is empty (only contains a module docstring). It is listed as a deliverable but contains no code. ADR-0007 requires "Flask-Login + Redis, no pwd_hash in session" -- the Flask-Login integration is actually in `extensions.py`, making `session.py` a dead file.

"""
ttrss_feeds — feed subscriptions with encrypted auth_pass (spec/02-database.md §Feed Management,

    # ADR-0009: In Python all auth_pass values are Fernet-encrypted; this flag tracks
    # whether PHP-era mcrypt encryption was already applied (migration marker).
    auth_pass_encrypted: Mapped[bool] = mapped_column(Boolean, nullable=False, default=False)

    @property
    def auth_pass(self) -> str:
        """
        Decrypt feed password from Fernet-encrypted column (ADR-0009, R11).
        Source: ttrss/include/crypt.php:decrypt_string (lines 2-20) → Fernet.decrypt()
        Returns empty string if column is empty (matches PHP default '').
        """
        if not self._auth_pass:
            return ""
        from ttrss.crypto.fernet import fernet_decrypt

        return fernet_decrypt(self._auth_pass)

    @auth_pass.setter
    def auth_pass(self, value: str | None) -> None:
        """
        Encrypt feed password before writing to column (ADR-0009, R11).
        Source: ttrss/include/crypt.php:encrypt_string (lines 22-29) → Fernet.encrypt()
        """
        if not value:
            self._auth_pass = ""
        else:
            from ttrss.crypto.fernet import fernet_encrypt

            self._auth_pass = fernet_encrypt(value)

Source: ttrss/schema/ttrss_schema_pgsql.sql (table ttrss_version, lines 262-264)
        + ttrss/classes/dbupdater.php:DbUpdater (schema version checking and migration)
        + ttrss/include/sanity_check.php (SCHEMA_VERSION=124 validation)
        + ttrss/include/functions.php:get_schema_version (line 988, runtime check)
        + ttrss/include/sessions.php:session_get_schema_version (line 26, session validation)

Seed data (line 264): INSERT INTO ttrss_version VALUES (124)
  → Python equivalent: Alembic migration baseline (ADR-0006).
"""
from sqlalchemy import Integer
from sqlalchemy.orm import Mapped, mapped_column

from ttrss.models.base import Base


# Source: ttrss/schema/ttrss_schema_pgsql.sql (table ttrss_version, lines 262-264)
# Deviation: schema_version used as primary_key=True because SQLAlchemy requires at least one PK.
# PHP schema defines "schema_version int not null" with no PK — this is a single-row table.
# Inferred from: PHP insert pattern (only one row ever exists) — PK is safe and idempotent.
class TtRssVersion(Base):
    """
    Single-row table tracking the current schema version.
    PHP constant: SCHEMA_VERSION = 124 (functions.php line 3).
    Queried by: get_schema_version() and session_get_schema_version().
    Python: Alembic replaces the PHP version-file upgrade mechanism.
    """

    __tablename__ = "ttrss_version"

    # Source: schema line 262 — schema_version int not null
    # Inferred PK: SQLAlchemy requires a primary key; PHP schema has none (single-row table).
    schema_version: Mapped[int] = mapped_column(Integer, primary_key=True)

```


## Assistant

**Tool Call: Write target\-repos/ttrss\-python/ttrss/blueprints/api/views.py**
Status: Completed

Diff: /Users/rd/devel/Capgemini/Capgemini_Internal/OSS_Migration/target-repos/ttrss-python/ttrss/blueprints/api/views.py
```
"""
TT-RSS REST API (/api/ — equivalent to PHP api/index.php).

Source: ttrss/api/index.php (bootstrap + dispatch, lines 1-74)
        + ttrss/classes/api.php:API (dispatch, wrap, login, logout, isLoggedIn, getVersion, getApiLevel)
        + ttrss/include/functions.php:authenticate_user (lines 706-795)

Protocol (spec/03-api-routing.md, R08, R09):
  POST or GET /api/ with JSON body (or query params for GET).
  Response envelope: {"seq": N, "status": 0|1, "content": {...}}
  seq MUST be echoed from the request in every response (CG-04).
  API level: 8.

Auth (ADR-0007, ADR-0008, R07, AR05):
  Login stores user_id in Redis session only — never pwd_hash (AR05).
  Legacy MODE2/SHA1X/SHA1 hashes are upgraded to argon2id on first successful login (ADR-0008).

CSRF (ADR-0002, spec/03-api-routing.md):
  The PHP API does NOT use CSRF tokens — it authenticates via session_id parameter.
  This blueprint is exempt from Flask-WTF CSRFProtect (see csrf.exempt below).
  Source: ttrss/api/index.php — no CSRF validation in API entry point.
"""
from flask import Blueprint, jsonify, request, session
from flask_login import current_user, login_user, logout_user

from ttrss.auth.password import hash_password, needs_upgrade, verify_password
from ttrss.extensions import csrf, db
from ttrss.models.user import TtRssUser

# Source: ttrss/api/index.php:1 (entry point), ttrss/classes/api.php:API (handler class)
api_bp = Blueprint("api", __name__, url_prefix="/api")

# Source: ttrss/api/index.php — PHP API has no CSRF protection (uses session_id tokens instead).
# New: csrf.exempt is required because Flask-WTF CSRFProtect is active globally (ADR-0002),
# but the API must remain CSRF-free for compatibility with PHP API clients.
csrf.exempt(api_bp)


def _seq() -> int:
    """
    Extract seq from request data — echoed in every response (CG-04, R08).
    Source: ttrss/classes/api.php:API.__construct (line 26: $this->seq = (int) $_REQUEST['seq'])
    Reads from JSON body first, then query params (matching PHP $_REQUEST merge order).
    """
    data = request.get_json(silent=True) or {}
    return int(data.get("seq", request.args.get("seq", 0)))


def _ok(seq: int, content: dict):
    """
    Success envelope. Source: ttrss/classes/api.php:API.wrap (lines 33-37, STATUS_OK=0).
    """
    return jsonify({"seq": seq, "status": 0, "content": content})


def _err(seq: int, error: str):
    """
    Error envelope. Source: ttrss/classes/api.php:API.wrap (lines 33-37, STATUS_ERR=1).
    """
    return jsonify({"seq": seq, "status": 1, "content": {"error": error}})


# Source: ttrss/api/index.php (method dispatch via $handler->$method())
#         + ttrss/classes/api.php:API (method routing)
@api_bp.route("/", methods=["GET", "POST"])
def dispatch():
    """Single dispatch endpoint for all API operations (spec/03-api-routing.md)."""
    data = request.get_json(silent=True) or {}
    op = data.get("op") or request.args.get("op", "")
    seq = _seq()

    if op == "login":
        return _handle_login(data, seq)
    if op == "logout":
        # Source: ttrss/classes/api.php:API.logout (lines 89-92)
        logout_user()
        session.clear()
        return _ok(seq, {"status": "OK"})
    if op == "isLoggedIn":
        # Source: ttrss/classes/api.php:API.isLoggedIn (lines 94-95)
        # PHP returns {"status":true/false} as boolean — preserved here.
        return _ok(seq, {"status": current_user.is_authenticated})
    if op == "getVersion":
        # Source: ttrss/classes/api.php:API.getVersion (lines 39-42)
        return _ok(seq, {"version": "1.12.0-python"})
    if op == "getApiLevel":
        # Source: ttrss/classes/api.php:API.getApiLevel (lines 44-47)
        return _ok(seq, {"level": 8})

    # Source: ttrss/classes/api.php:API.__call (line 488 — UNKNOWN_METHOD error)
    return _err(seq, "UNKNOWN_METHOD")


def _handle_login(data: dict, seq: int):
    """
    Authenticate user and create session.
    Upgrades legacy MODE2/SHA1X/SHA1 hash to argon2id on successful login (ADR-0008, R10).
    Session stores user_id only — never pwd_hash (ADR-0007, R07, AR05).
    Response includes session_id and api_level=8 (R08, spec/03-api-routing.md).

    Source: ttrss/classes/api.php:API.login (lines 49-88)
            + ttrss/include/functions.php:authenticate_user (lines 706-755)
            + ttrss/plugins/auth_internal/init.php:Auth_Internal::authenticate (lines 19-140)
    """
    username = data.get("user", "")
    password = data.get("password", "")

    # Source: ttrss/plugins/auth_internal/init.php:authenticate — SELECT login, pwd_hash, salt
    user: TtRssUser | None = db.session.scalars(
        db.select(TtRssUser).where(TtRssUser.login == username)
    ).first()

    if not user or not verify_password(
        user.pwd_hash,
        password,
        salt=user.salt or "",
        login=user.login,
    ):
        # Source: ttrss/classes/api.php:API.login (line 68 — "LOGIN_ERROR")
        return _err(seq, "LOGIN_ERROR")

    # Upgrade legacy hash to argon2id on first successful login (ADR-0008)
    # Source: ttrss/plugins/auth_internal/init.php:authenticate (lines 91-101 — MODE2 upgrade logic)
    if needs_upgrade(user.pwd_hash):
        user.pwd_hash = hash_password(password)
        user.salt = ""  # argon2id embeds its own salt; ttrss_users.salt no longer needed
        # Note: salt column is NOT NULL default '' in PHP schema (line 49) — use "" not None
        db.session.commit()

    # Source: ttrss/include/functions.php:authenticate_user (lines 724-739 — session setup)
    login_user(user)
    # AR05: store only user_id — pwd_hash MUST NOT be stored in session
    # (contrast with PHP: $_SESSION["pwd_hash"] = ... — deliberately NOT replicated)
    session["user_id"] = user.id

    return _ok(
        seq,
        {
            "session_id": getattr(session, "sid", ""),  # Flask-Session sets .sid
            "api_level": 8,
        },
    )

```

```
"""
TT-RSS AJAX RPC dispatcher (/backend.php — equivalent to PHP backend.php).

Source: ttrss/backend.php (entry point) + ttrss/classes/backend.php:Backend (dispatch class)
        + ttrss/classes/handler/protected.php (login_required base for all backend ops)
Phase 1a: stub dispatcher only. Full op→handler routing in Phase 1b.

CSRF (R13, ADR-0002, AR06):
  Flask-WTF CSRFProtect is active globally.
  Config WTF_CSRF_HEADERS=["X-CSRFToken","X-CSRF-Token"] allows AJAX callers
  to pass the token as a header (A-NC-05, CG-05).
  JavaScript must include X-CSRFToken in all state-mutating POST requests.
"""
from flask import Blueprint, jsonify, request
from flask_login import login_required

# Source: ttrss/backend.php + ttrss/classes/backend.php:Backend
backend_bp = Blueprint("backend", __name__)


# Source: ttrss/backend.php (POST handler) + ttrss/classes/handler/protected.php (login guard)
@backend_bp.post("/backend.php")
@login_required
def dispatch():
    """
    Phase 1a stub. CSRF enforced globally by Flask-WTF CSRFProtect (R13).
    Full handler dispatch (op=feeds, rpc, article, pref-*, etc.) in Phase 1b.

    Source: ttrss/backend.php reads from $_REQUEST (merges GET+POST+COOKIE).
    Python: reads from form data, JSON body, AND query params to match PHP $_REQUEST.
    """
    data = request.get_json(silent=True) or {}
    # Source: ttrss/backend.php — PHP $_REQUEST merges GET, POST, COOKIE.
    # Read op/method from form, JSON, or query params to match PHP behavior.
    op = request.form.get("op") or data.get("op") or request.args.get("op", "")
    method = request.form.get("method") or data.get("method") or request.args.get("method", "")
    return jsonify({"op": op, "method": method, "status": "PHASE_1A_STUB"})

```

"""
Application configuration (R03, ADR-0002, AR01).
All values read from environment variables via os.environ.get().
Set env vars BEFORE importing this module (Config class attributes are
evaluated at class definition / import time).

Inferred from: ttrss/config.php-dist (TTRSS_SELF_URL_PATH, DB_HOST, DB_NAME, DB_PASS,
               SESSION_COOKIE_LIFETIME, SESSION_CHECK_ADDRESS, FEED_CRYPT_KEY, etc.)
               Adapted for 12-factor env var pattern — no static PHP constants.
New: Config class with os.environ.get() (no direct PHP equivalent)
"""
import os

from redis import Redis


# Inferred from: ttrss/config.php-dist (all DEFINE constants), adapted for Flask + 12-factor
class Config:
    """Production / development configuration."""

    # New: Flask requires SECRET_KEY for session signing — no PHP equivalent
    SECRET_KEY: str = os.environ.get("SECRET_KEY", "")

    # Inferred from: ttrss/config.php-dist:DB_HOST, DB_NAME, DB_USER, DB_PASS, DB_TYPE (lines 6-11)
    SQLALCHEMY_DATABASE_URI: str = os.environ.get("DATABASE_URL", "")
    # New: Flask-SQLAlchemy setting — disables modification tracking for performance
    SQLALCHEMY_TRACK_MODIFICATIONS: bool = False
    # New: SQLAlchemy pool_pre_ping ensures stale connections are recycled
    SQLALCHEMY_ENGINE_OPTIONS: dict = {"pool_pre_ping": True}

    # Inferred from: ttrss/config.php-dist:FEED_CRYPT_KEY (line 27, same constant name)
    # Stored as bytes for Fernet() constructor (ADR-0009)
    FEED_CRYPT_KEY: bytes = os.environ.get("FEED_CRYPT_KEY", "").encode()

    # Flask-Session — Redis backend (ADR-0007, R07, CG-07)
    # Inferred from: ttrss/include/sessions.php (PHP native sessions replaced by Redis)
    # New: SESSION_TYPE="redis" — PHP used custom DB-backed sessions (ttrss_sessions table)
    SESSION_TYPE: str = "redis"
    SESSION_REDIS: Redis = Redis.from_url(
        os.environ.get("REDIS_URL", "redis://localhost:6379/0")
    )
    # New: session signing prevents session ID forgery (no PHP equivalent)
    SESSION_USE_SIGNER: bool = True
    # New: HttpOnly prevents JS access to session cookie (spec/06-security.md F10)
    SESSION_COOKIE_HTTPONLY: bool = True
    # New: SameSite=Lax prevents CSRF via cross-origin requests (spec/06-security.md)
    SESSION_COOKIE_SAMESITE: str = "Lax"
    # Inferred from: ttrss/config.php-dist:SESSION_COOKIE_LIFETIME (line 144, default 86400)
    SESSION_COOKIE_LIFETIME: int = int(
        os.environ.get("SESSION_COOKIE_LIFETIME", "86400")
    )

    # Flask-WTF CSRF (R13, ADR-0002)
    # New: CSRF tokens replace PHP custom uniqid() tokens (spec/06-security.md F6)
    WTF_CSRF_ENABLED: bool = True
    # New: X-CSRFToken header enables CSRF for AJAX RPC calls (backend.php equivalent)
    WTF_CSRF_HEADERS: list = ["X-CSRFToken", "X-CSRF-Token"]

```

"""
Flask extension objects (ADR-0002, ADR-0007, R01, AR02).
Defined without an app; init_app() called in create_app().

Source: ttrss/classes/db.php:Db (singleton DB pattern)
        + ttrss/include/sessions.php (PHP native sessions)
        + ttrss/include/functions.php:authenticate_user / login_sequence (auth flow)
        Adapted for Flask extension pattern — init_app() replaces PHP global singletons.
New: LoginManager, Session, CSRFProtect, Talisman (no direct PHP equivalents)
"""
from flask_login import LoginManager
from flask_session import Session
from flask_sqlalchemy import SQLAlchemy
from flask_talisman import Talisman
from flask_wtf.csrf import CSRFProtect

from ttrss.models.base import Base

# Source: ttrss/classes/db.php:Db (singleton pattern)
# Python equivalent: Flask-SQLAlchemy extension; model_class=Base ensures single metadata
# so Alembic sees all tables (A-NC-02/03)
db = SQLAlchemy(model_class=Base)

# Inferred from: ttrss/include/sessions.php:validate_session + ttrss/include/functions.php:login_sequence
# Flask-Login replaces PHP $_SESSION["uid"] + validate_session() pattern (ADR-0007)
login_manager = LoginManager()

# Inferred from: ttrss/include/sessions.php (PHP native sessions replaced by Redis, ADR-0007)
sess = Session()

# New: CSRF protection — replaces PHP custom uniqid() tokens (spec/06-security.md F6, R13)
csrf = CSRFProtect()

# New: security headers — no PHP equivalent (spec/06-security.md F7: missing security headers)
# Adds HSTS, X-Content-Type-Options, X-Frame-Options per ADR-0002 security requirements.
talisman = Talisman()

# New: Flask-Login login_view — redirects unauthenticated users to public index.
# PHP equivalent: login_sequence() in functions.php redirects to public.php.
login_manager.login_view = "public.index"  # type: ignore[assignment]


# Inferred from: ttrss/include/sessions.php:validate_session (user lookup by session uid)
# Source: ttrss/include/sessions.php (lines 77-92 — uid-based session validation)
@login_manager.user_loader
def load_user(user_id: str):
    # Lazy import prevents circular import: extensions → models.user → models.base (AR02)
    from ttrss.models.user import TtRssUser

    return db.session.get(TtRssUser, int(user_id))

```


**Tool Call: Write target\-repos/ttrss\-python/ttrss/errors.py**
